                  <foreign lang="ar">حُمْرَةٌ</foreign>, the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">حُمْرٌ</foreign> (S, Msb) and <foreign lang="ar">حُمْرَانٌ</foreign>; for you say <foreign lang="ar">ثِيَابٌ حُمْرٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">حُمْرَانٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">red garments</hi>]: (TA:) but if you apply it as an epithet to a man, [in which case it has other meanings than those explained above, as will be shown in what follows,] the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">أَحَامِرُ</foreign> (S) and <foreign lang="ar">حُمْرٌ</foreign>: (TA:) or if it means <hi rend="ital">a thing having the colour termed</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">حُمْرَةٌ</foreign>, the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">أَحَامِرُ</foreign>, because, in this case, it is a subst., not an epithet. (Msb.)   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n9085-2" target="أَحْمَرِىٌّ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n9086"/></foreign> also signifies the same as <foreign lang="ar">أَحْمَرُ</foreign>: (Ham p. 379:) or, as some say, it has an intensive sense. (TA voce <foreign lang="ar">كَرُوبِيُّونَ</foreign>.) It is said in the S, in art. <foreign lang="ar">دك</foreign>, that <foreign lang="ar">حَمْرَاوَاتٌ</foreign> is a pl. of <foreign lang="ar">حَمْرَآءُ</foreign>, like as <foreign lang="ar">دَكَّاوَاتٌ</foreign>, is of <foreign lang="ar">دَكَّآءُ</foreign>; but it is not so. (IB in that art.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Applied to a camel, <hi rend="ital">Of a colour like that of saffron when a garment is dyed with it so that it stands up by reason of</hi> [<hi rend="ital">the thickness of</hi>] <hi rend="ital">the dye:</hi> (TA:) or <hi rend="ital">of an unmixed red colour;</hi> (As, S in art. <foreign lang="ar">كمت</foreign>, and TA;) and so the fem. when applied to a she-goat. (TA.) It is said that, of she-camels, the <foreign lang="ar">حَمْرَآء</foreign> is the most able to endure the summer midday-heat; and the <foreign lang="ar">وَرْقَآء</foreign>, to endure nightjourneying; and that the <foreign lang="ar">صَهْبَآء</foreign> is the most notable and the most beautiful to look at: so said Aboo-Nasr En-Na'ámee: and the Arabs say that the best of camels are the <foreign lang="ar">حُمْر</foreign> and the <foreign lang="ar">صُهْب</foreign>. (TA.) [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">حُمْرُ النَّعَمِ</foreign> signifies <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The high-bred,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">excellent, of camels:</hi> and is proverbially applied to <pb n="642"/> 
                  <hi rend="ital">anything highly prized, precious, valuable,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">excellent.</hi> (Mgh, Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  Applied to a man, (AA, Sh, Az,) <hi rend="ital">White</hi> (AA, Sh, Az, K) <hi rend="ital">in complexion;</hi> (Az;) because <foreign lang="ar">أَبْيَضُ</foreign> might be considered as of evil omen [implying the meaning of leprosy]: (AA, Sh:) or, accord. to Th, because the latter epithet, applied to a man, was only used by the Arabs as signifying “ pure, ” or “ free from faults: ” but they sometimes used this latter epithet in the sense of “ white in complexion, ” applied to a man &amp;c.: (IAth:) fem., in the same sense, <foreign lang="ar">حَمْرَآءُ</foreign>: the dim. of which,   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n9085-3" target="حُمَيْرَآءُ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n9075"/></foreign>, occurs in a trad., applied to 'Áïsheh. (K, * TA.) So, accord. to some, in the trad., <foreign lang="ar">بُعِثْتُ إِلَى الأَحْمَرِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَالأَسْوَدِ</foreign>, (TA,) i. e. <hi rend="ital">I have been sent to the white and the black;</hi> because these two epithets comprise all mankind: (Az, TA:) [therefore, by the former we should understand the white and the red races; and by the latter, the negroes: but some hold that by the former are meant the foreigners, and] by the latter are meant the Arabs. (TA.) One says also, [when speaking of Arabs and more northern races,] <foreign lang="ar">أَتَانِى كُلُّ أَسْوَدَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مِنْهُمْ وَأَحْمَرَ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">Every Arab of them, and foreigner, came to me:</hi> and one should not say, in this sense, <foreign lang="ar">أَبْيَضَ</foreign>. (AA, As, S.) <foreign lang="ar">الحَمْرَآءُ</foreign>, also, is applied to <hi rend="ital">The foreigners</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">العَجَمُ</foreign>) [<hi rend="ital">collectively</hi>]; (S, A, K;) because a reddish white is the prevailing hue of their complexion: (S:) or <hi rend="ital">the Persians and Greeks:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">those foreigners mostly characterized by whiteness of complexion; as the Greeks and Persians.</hi> (TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَ فِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الحَمْرَآءِ مِثْلُهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">There is not among the foreigners</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">العَجَم</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">the like of him.</hi> (A.) And accord. to some, <foreign lang="ar">الأَحْمَرُ وَالأَبْيَضُ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">The Arabs and the foreigners.</hi> (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">الحَمْرَآءُ</foreign> [so in the TA, but correctly <foreign lang="ar">أَبْنَآءُ الحَمْرَآءِ</foreign>,] is an appellation applied to <hi rend="ital">Emancipated slaves:</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">اِبْنُ حَمْرَآءِ العِجَانِ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">Son of the female slave,</hi> is an appellation used in reviling and blaming. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  Also <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  A man <hi rend="ital">having no weapons with him:</hi> pl. <foreign lang="ar">حُمْرٌ</foreign> (A, K) and <foreign lang="ar">حُمْرَانٌ</foreign>. (K.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">الحُسْنُ أَحْمَرُ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">Beauty is in</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الحُمْرَة</foreign> [app. <hi rend="ital">fairness of complexion;</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">beauty is fair-complexioned</hi>]: (TA:) or <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">beauty is attended by difficulty;</hi> i. e. he who loves beauty must bear difficulty, or distress: (IAth:) or the lover experiences from beauty what is experienced from war. (ISd, K.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">الأَحْمَرُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">A sort of dates:</hi> (K:) so called because of their colour. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">الأَحْمَرُ وَالأَبْيَضُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Gold and silver.</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">الأَحْمَرَانِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Flesh-meat and wine;</hi> (S, A, K;) said to destroy men: (S:) so in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">نَحْنُ مِنْ أَهْلِ الأَسْوَدَيْنِ لَا الأَحْمَرَيْنِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">We are of the people of dates and water, not of flesh-meat and wine:</hi> (A:) or <hi rend="ital">the beverage called</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">نَبِيذ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">and flesh-meat.</hi> (IAar.) Also <hi rend="ital">Wine and</hi> [<hi rend="ital">garments of the kind called</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">بُرُود</foreign>. (Sh.) And <hi rend="ital">Gold and saffron;</hi> (Az, ISd, K;) said to destroy women; i. e. the love of ornaments and perfumes destroys them: (Az:) or these are called <foreign lang="ar">الأَصْفَرَانِ</foreign>; (AO, TA;) and milk and water, <foreign lang="ar">الأَبْيَضَانِ</foreign>; (TA;) and dates and water, <foreign lang="ar">الأَسْوَدَانِ</foreign>. (As.)          <sense type="b" n="9">-b9-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">وَطْأَةٌ حَمْرَآءُ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">A new,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">recent, footstep,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">footprint:</hi> opposed to <foreign lang="ar">دَهْمَآءُ</foreign>. (As, S, A.)          <sense type="b" n="10">-b10-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">سَنَةٌ حَمْرَآءُ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">A severe year;</hi> (S, K;) because it is a mean between the <foreign lang="ar">سَوْدَآء</foreign> and the <foreign lang="ar">بَيْضآء</foreign>: or <hi rend="ital">a year of severe drought;</hi> because, in such a year, the tracts of the horizon are red: (TA:) when <foreign lang="ar">الجَبْهَةُ</foreign> [the tenth Mansion of the Moon (see <foreign lang="ar">مَنَازِلُ القَمَرِ</foreign> in art. <foreign lang="ar">نزل</foreign>)] breaks its promise [of bringing rain], the year is such as is thus called. (AHn.)          <sense type="b" n="11">-b11-</sense>  See also <foreign lang="ar">حَمْرَآءُ</foreign> voce <foreign lang="ar">حَمَارَّةٌ</foreign>.          <sense type="b" n="12">-b12-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">جَآءَ بِغَنَمِهِ حُمْرَ الكُلَى</foreign>, and, in like manner, <foreign lang="ar">سُودَ البُطُونِ</foreign>, <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He brought his sheep</hi> or <hi rend="ital">goats, in a lean,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an emaciated, state.</hi> (A, * TA.)    </entryFree>32:T962,<entryFree id="n9088" key="مِحْمَرٌ" type="main">
